                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{eqnarray}{D}_{\rm Na} {}^+ = \frac{4}{{\pi \tau }}{\left( {\frac{{{m}_B{V}_M}}{{{M}_BS}}} \right)}^2{\left( {\frac{{\Delta {E}_S}}{{\Delta {E}_\tau }}} \right)}^2\end{eqnarray}$$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(1)</span></div>Where <i>τ</i> is the excitation current time (s); <i>m<sub>B</sub></i>, <i>M<sub>B</sub></i>, and <i>V<sub>M</sub></i> are the mass (g), molecular weight (g&nbsp;mol<sup>−1</sup>), and molar volume (cm<sup>3</sup>&nbsp;mol<sup>−1</sup>) of the HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO, respectively; <i>S</i> is the electrode area (cm<sup>2</sup>); <i>∆E<sub>S</sub></i> is steady state voltage change, <i>∆E<sub><i>τ</i></sub></i> is the transient voltage variable. Using a pulse current of 0.14&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the charge-discharge time is 10&nbsp;min, and it is left to stand for 30&nbsp;min. Benefiting from the interlayer spacing expansion effect of organic aliphatic diamines, the <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> of HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF fluctuates in the range of 10<sup>−8</sup> to 10<sup>−10</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>, showing fast Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics and outperforms most of vanadium-based materials (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0048_R_d217230257e1404" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Adv. Energy Mater.">48</a>, <a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0050_R_d217230257e1404" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Energy Storage Mater.">50</a>, <a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0052_R_d217230257e1404" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Adv. Energy Mater.">52</a>, <a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0059" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0059_R_d217230257e1404" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 59 - ACS Nano">59</a>, <a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0063_R_d217230257e1404" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - Energy Storage Mater.">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></div>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">To further reveal their electrochemical reaction kinetics, the capacitive charge storage and diffusion control processes of the PDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO, BDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO, and HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO hybrid electrodes are comprehensively evaluated by measuring the CV curves at different scan rates. The results are shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202303102-fig-0005">5</a>. As the scan rate increases from 0.2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> to 1.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, the CV curves show a similar shape, and a gradually increasing peak intensity can be seen (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202303102-fig-0005">5a–c</a>). In the CV curves, the peak current and scan rate follow the following rules :<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0064" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0064_R_d217230257e1424" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 64 - ACS Nano">64</a>, <a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0065_R_d217230257e1424" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 65 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">65</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup><div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202303102-disp-0002"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                     <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/f3d97e81-dc8c-4e13-825b-76be4591081f/adfm202303102-math-0002.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202303102:adfm202303102-math-0002" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202303102-math-0002.png">
                        <semantics>
                           <mtable displaystyle="true">
                              <mtr>
                                 <mtd columnalign="right">
                                    <mrow>
                                       <mi>i</mi>
                                       <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                                       <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                                       <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                                       <mi>a</mi>
                                       <msup>
                                          <mi>v</mi>
                                          <mi>b</mi>
                                       </msup>
                                    </mrow>
                                 </mtd>
                              </mtr>
                           </mtable>
                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{eqnarray}i\ = \ a{v}^b\end{eqnarray}$$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(2)</span></div>Where <i>i</i> is the peak current, <i>v</i> is the scan rate, and <i>a</i> and <i>b</i> are variable parameters. <i>b</i> value of 0.5 indicates a semi-infinite diffusion mechanism, while <i>b</i> value of 1.0 indicates capacitive behavior.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0039_R_d217230257e1462" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Energy Environ. Sci">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In our work, the <i>b</i> values of PDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF (7.7&nbsp;Å), BDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF (8.1&nbsp;Å) and HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF (8.9&nbsp;Å) are 0.66, 0.75, and 0.81 (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11a–c</a>, Supporting Information), respectively, indicating that there are both diffusion control and capacitive control during Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction. In addition, the contribution ratio of capacitive to the total capacity can be calculated according to the following equation:

               <div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202303102-disp-0003"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                     <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/98b13e91-cd15-41e9-93b3-1f1c0cd4c168/adfm202303102-math-0003.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202303102:adfm202303102-math-0003" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202303102-math-0003.png">
                        <semantics>
                           <mtable displaystyle="true">
                              <mtr>
                                 <mtd columnalign="right">
                                    <mrow>
                                       <mi>i</mi>
                                       <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                                       <mfenced close=")" open="(">
                                          <mi>V</mi>
                                       </mfenced>
                                       <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                                       <msub>
                                          <mi>k</mi>
                                          <mn>1</mn>
                                       </msub>
                                       <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                                       <mi>v</mi>
                                       <mo linebreak="goodbreak">+</mo>
                                       <msub>
                                          <mi>k</mi>
                                          <mn>2</mn>
                                       </msub>
                                       <msup>
                                          <mi>v</mi>
                                          <mrow>
                                             <mn>1</mn>
                                             <mo>/</mo>
                                             <mn>2</mn>
                                          </mrow>
                                       </msup>
                                    </mrow>
                                 </mtd>
                              </mtr>
                           </mtable>
                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{eqnarray}i\ \left( V \right) = {k}_1\ v + {k}_2{v}^{1/2}\end{eqnarray}$$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(3)</span></div>where <i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>v</i> and <i>k</i><sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> are the assigned values for the capacitive and diffusion control processes, respectively. The capacitive contributions at different scan rates are calculated as in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202303102-fig-0005">5d–f</a>. The capacitive contribution of HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF electrode is 70.9%, 76.1%, 80.6%, 85.1%, and 93.0% at scan rate of 0.2, 0.4, 0.6, 0.8, and 1.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, which is mostly higher than that of PDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF (59.1%, 73.0%, 81.5%, 83.3%, and 88.3% at 0.2, 0.4, 0.6, 0.8, and 1.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, respectively) and BDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF (56.5%, 73.9%, 77.6%, 80.0%, and 88.9% at 0.2, 0.4, 0.6, 0.8, and 1.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, respectively) (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11d–f</a>, Supporting Information). It is proved that the higher specific capacity of HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF is mainly due to the domination of capacitive behavior. At a scan rate of 0.2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF has a high specific capacity of 474&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, consisting of capacitive contribution of 336&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and the remaining 138&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> of diffusion contribution, which is close to the XPS result of HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO (147&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). Furthermore, as the scan rate increases, the percentage of capacitive contribution of each specimen also increases. The increased capacitive contribution leads to a large amount of Na<sup>+</sup> storage on the active material surface with less structural collapse, which is beneficial for the fast Na<sup>+</sup> transport and structural stabilization.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0066" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0066_R_d217230257e1547" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 66 - Small">66</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></div>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202303102-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/a0f7895e-dde1-4153-9c2b-a301582d3792/adfm202303102-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/a0f7895e-dde1-4153-9c2b-a301582d3792/adfm202303102-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/0cca5a84-8cfd-4d54-858f-d597c7bc2a79/adfm202303102-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/a0f7895e-dde1-4153-9c2b-a301582d3792/adfm202303102-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202303102-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202303102" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">CV curves of a) PDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO, b) BDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO and c) HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO at different scan rates. Capacitive contribution of d) PDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO, e) BDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO and f) HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO at various scan rates.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>First-principles density functional theory (DFT) simulations are performed to in-depth uncover the roles of pre-intercalated organic aliphatic diamine molecule with PDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO, BDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO, and HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO as typical models. As we know, energy storage capability is firstly related to the number of accommodated ions inside the materials. As shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202303102-fig-0006">6a–c</a>, benefiting from having more active sites and larger interlayer spacing to accommodate more Na<sup>+</sup> ions, BDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO and HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO provide a theoretical specific capacity of 259 and 248&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, much higher than that of PDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO (183&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). Meanwhile, transport kinetics of ions within bulk materials is another key factor that determines the electrochemical performance of the electrode materials. When Na atoms diffuse between two adjacent V<span class="icomoon"></span>O layers along the optimal O<span class="icomoon"></span>B pathway (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information), the migration energy barrier of Na in HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO is 0.67&nbsp;eV, much lower than those of PDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO (0.98&nbsp;eV) and BDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO (0.73&nbsp;eV) due to having wide open ion diffusion channels with larger interlayer spacing (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202303102-fig-0006">6d–f</a>). The synergy effect of more active sites and larger interlayer spacing endows HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO with the largest specific capacity, which matches well with the experimental results.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202303102-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/5b788793-bc05-4276-a271-357a4a146c72/adfm202303102-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/5b788793-bc05-4276-a271-357a4a146c72/adfm202303102-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/22af2963-0c78-47cb-966e-171c70b65c10/adfm202303102-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/5b788793-bc05-4276-a271-357a4a146c72/adfm202303102-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202303102-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202303102" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The simulated redox active sites and theoretical redox capacity of a) PDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO, b) BDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO and c) HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO. Simulated migration energy barrier of Na ions in d) PDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO, e) BDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO and f) HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO with the O<span class="icomoon"></span>B direction of the cell.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202303102-sec-0060">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202303102-sec-0060-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, we exploit a facile strategy to synthesize 2D layered vanadium oxides with tunable interlayer spacing through using organic aliphatic diamines with various chain length as structural orientation agent. The interaction between the terminal doubly protonated amine and the V<span class="icomoon"></span>O layer endows the pre-intercalated organic aliphatic diamine molecule to be a stable intermediate layer column, which expands the Na<sup>+</sup> transport channel and ensures fast electrochemical kinetics of Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion (10<sup>−8</sup> to 10<sup>−10</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>). The optimized SIB based on the first synthesized HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF hybrid electrode obtains a high specific capacity of 597&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and exhibits superb cycling stability (with only 0.051% capacity decay per cycle at 10&nbsp;C). Meanwhile, DFT calculation also proves that the [V<sub>6</sub>O<sub>14</sub>] lamellar structure is favorable for increasing the active sites and reducing the energy barrier for Na<sup>+</sup> transport. This strategy can provide a functionally oriented methodology for the synthesis of 2D layered materials with tunable interlayer spacing.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202303102-sec-0070">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202303102-sec-0070-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202303102-sec-0080">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202303102-sec-0090">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202303102-sec-0100">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202303102-sec-0100-title"> Fabrication of DA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF Hybrid Electrodes</h4>
                  
                  <p>The synthesis of (H<sub>3</sub>N(CH<sub>2</sub>)<sub>6</sub>NH<sub>3</sub>)[V<sub>6</sub>O<sub>14</sub>]/NF (HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF) hybrid electrode was carried out in a conventional solvothermal method. To be specific, V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub> (0.15&nbsp;g), 1,6-hexanediamine (0.0941&nbsp;g) and deionized (DI) water (15&nbsp;mL) was mixed and transferred to Teflon-lined autoclave (20&nbsp;mL). A piece of Ni foam current collector, cleaned by immersing in acetone and 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> hydrochloric acid for 10&nbsp;min successively to remove the residual organic species and surface oxide layer, was laid into the Teflon-lined autoclave and maintained at 180&nbsp;°C for 24&nbsp;h. After cooling to room temperature, the resultant was washed with water and anhydrous ethanol and dried under vacuum at 60&nbsp;°C overnight. (H<sub>3</sub>N(CH<sub>2</sub>)<sub>3</sub>NH<sub>3</sub>)[V<sub>4</sub>O<sub>10</sub>] (PDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO) and (H<sub>3</sub>N(CH<sub>2</sub>)<sub>4</sub>NH<sub>3</sub>)[V<sub>6</sub>O<sub>14</sub>] (BDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO) were synthesized using a similar way with modulation. The feedstocks were V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub> (0.15&nbsp;g), 1,3-propanediamine (0.06&nbsp;g), DI water (15&nbsp;mL) for PDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub> (0.1242&nbsp;g), 1,4-butanediamine (0.06&nbsp;g), DI water (15&nbsp;mL) for BDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0067" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0067_R_d217230257e1715" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 67 - Mater. Res. Bull.">67</a>, <a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0068" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0068_R_d217230257e1715" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 68 - J. Solid State Chem.">68</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The CCDC number for PDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO, BDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO, and HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO was 1 314 595,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0069" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0069_R_d217230257e1720" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 69 - Chem. Mater.">69</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> 657 487<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0038_R_d217230257e1726" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - J. Inorg. Organomet. Polym.">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and 2 193 696, respectively.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202303102-sec-0110">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202303102-sec-0110-title"> Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>The powder X-ray diffraction patterns were measured by Rigaku D/max-HB powder diffractometer with Cu target K<i>α</i>-ray (<i>λ</i>&nbsp;=&nbsp;1.5418&nbsp;Å). The microstructure of the specimens was investigated using a field-emission scanning electron microscope (Hitachi SU-8010, 3&nbsp;kV) and transmission electron microscope (JEOL-2100F, JEM-F 200, and 200&nbsp;kV). Prodigy Leeman ICP-AES detector was used for elemental content testing. Thermogravimetric analyzer (SDT Q600) was used for the determination under air atmosphere with a temperature increase rate of 10°C&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup>. The structural information of the specimens was analyzed by Fourier infrared spectroscopy (BRUKE Vertex 70, 0.4&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>, 400–4000&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>) and Raman spectra (Labram HR 800). Crystal data collection was performed using a Bruker SMARTt APEX II CCD X-ray diffractometer (Mo target K<i>α</i> rays, <i>λ</i>&nbsp;=&nbsp;0.71073&nbsp;Å) and the structure was solved with the SHELXT <sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0002_R_d217230257e1755" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Adv. Mater.">2</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> structure solution program using Intrinsic Phasing and refined with the SHELXL <sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0003_R_d217230257e1760" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Adv. Mater.">3</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> refinement package using Least Squares minimization. The surface elements and electronic states were determined using a KRATOS Axis ultra DLD X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS, Mg target K<i>α</i> ray, 1283.3&nbsp;eV).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202303102-sec-0120">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202303102-sec-0120-title"> Battery Assembly and Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>A series of coin-type sodium ion batteries (CR2025) were assembled in a dry glove box filled with argon (moisture and oxygen levels were kept below 0.01&nbsp;ppm), with PDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF, BDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF, and HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO/NF as working electrodes, sodium foil as counter/reference electrode, glass microfiber septum (GF/A, Whatman) as separator, and 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaClO<sub>4</sub> dissolved in ethylene carbonate (EC): dimethyl carbonate (DMC): ethyl methyl carbonate (EMC)&nbsp;=&nbsp;1:1:1 as electrolyte. CV and EIS were tested on a Squidstat electrochemical analysis instrument in the voltage range of 0.01 and 3&nbsp;V (versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na). The rate capability and cycling performance were tested on a Land battery test system.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202303102-sec-0130">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202303102-sec-0130-title"> Calculation Method</h4>
                  
                  <p>First-principles DFT simulations were performed using the VASP package. The electron exchange-correlation (XC) energies were treated by the generalized gradient approximation (GGA) in the Perdew Burke Ernzerhof (PBE) scheme.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0070" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0070_R_d217230257e1792" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 70 - Phys. Rev. Lett.">70</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, the projection enhanced wave (PAW) pseudopotential was used to describe the ion nucleus and valence electron interactions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0071" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0071_R_d217230257e1797" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 71 - Phys. Rev. B">71</a>, <a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0072" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0072_R_d217230257e1797" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 72 - Phys. Rev. B">72</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> A kinetic energy cutoff of 450&nbsp;eV was chosen as the plane wave basis set. All structural models were analyzed by single crystal X-ray and were fully optimized until the force was less than 10<sup>−2</sup>&nbsp;eV&nbsp;Å<sup>−1</sup> and the energy converged to 10<sup>−5</sup>&nbsp;<i>e</i>V between two consecutive self-consistent steps. A vacuum space of 15&nbsp;Å was applied perpendicular to the slab to reduce the effect of interactions induced by periodic images. The integration over the reciprocal space was performed using a Monkhorst model with a 1&nbsp;×&nbsp;1&nbsp;×&nbsp;1&nbsp;K-point grid. The migration behavior of Na in different regions of the model was evaluated using the climbing-image NEB method.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202303102-bib-0073" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202303102-bib-0073_R_d217230257e1811" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 73 - J. Chem. Phys.">73</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
                  
                  <p>[CCDC-2193696 (HDA<span class="icomoon"></span>VO) contains the supplementary crystallographic data for this paper. These data can be obtained free of charge from The Cambridge Crystallographic Data Centre via <a href="http://www.ccdc.cam.ac.uk/data_request/cif" class="linkBehavior">www.ccdc.cam.ac.uk/data_request/cif</a>.]</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
